## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms

# Task: Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/kubernetes--8c9c67c0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a subsystem architecture guide for kubelet container manager, including resource manager interactions and platform variance.

## Scope

Focus on the kubelet container manager subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

When remapping internal\\n59: \\t\\t// names to systemd cgroup driver, we want to remap \\\"-\\\" => \\\"_\\\",\\n60: \\t\\t// so we forbid \\\"_\\\" so that we can always reverse the mapping.\\n61: \\t\\tif strings.Contains(component, \\\"/\\\") || strings.Contains(component, \\\"_\\\") {\\n62: \\t\\t\\tpanic(fmt.Errorf(\\\"invalid character in component [%q] of CgroupName\\\", component))\\n63: \\t\\t}\\n64: \\t}\\n65: \\treturn CgroupName(append(append([]string{}, base...), components...))\\n66: }\\n67: \\n68: func escapeSystemdCgroupName(part string) string {\\n69: \\treturn strings.Replace(part, \\\"-\\\", \\\"_\\\", -1)\\n70: }\\n71: \\n72: func unescapeSystemdCgroupName(part string) string {\\n73: \\treturn strings.Replace(part, \\\"_\\\", \\\"-\\\", -1)\\n74: }\\n75: \\n76: // cgroupName.ToSystemd converts the internal cgroup name to a systemd name.\\n77: // For example, the name {\\\"kubepods\\\", \\\"burstable\\\", \\\"pod1234-abcd-5678-efgh\\\"} becomes\\n78: // \\\"/kubepods.slice/kubepods-burstable.slice/kubepods-burstable-pod1234_abcd_5678_efgh.slice\\\"\\n79: // This function always expands the systemd name into the cgroupfs form. {
  "content": "# Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nThe kubelet container manager subsystem is responsible for managing container resources, enforcing Quality of Service (QoS) classes, and coordinating resource allocation across CPU, memory, and device plugins. It sits at the intersection of pod scheduling, container runtime execution, and system resource enforcement on the node.\n\nThe container manager operates at several levels:\n- **System level**: Managing system containers and daemon processes\n- **Node level**: Enforcing node allocatable reservations and capacity limits\n- **Pod level**: Creating pod cgroups and managing QoS hierarchies\n- **Container level**: Allocating exclusive resources and updating runtime constraints\n\n## Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\nThe container manager ensures that:\n1. Container resource requests and limits are enforced through cgroup mechanisms\n2. Resources are allocated according to pod QoS classes (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort)\n3. Topology-aware resource allocation is coordinated across multiple resource managers\n4. Device plugins can register and provide custom resources\n5. Dynamic resource allocation can be managed through DRA framework\n6. System services and kubelet process have protected resource reservations\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies:**\n- **Kubelet Core** (`pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go`): Initializes the container manager during startup and calls it for pod admission and container lifecycle hooks\n- **Pod Workers** (`pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`): Request container lifecycle operations through the manager\n- **Runtime Service** (CRI): Container manager updates container resources through CRI calls to adjust CPU/memory constraints\n- **cAdvisor** (`pkg/kubelet/cadvisor/`): Provides machine topology and filesystem capacity information\n\n**Downstream Dependents:**\n- **Pod Container Manager** (`pkg/kubelet/cm/`): Manages pod-level cgroups based on QoS class\n- **Resource Managers**: CPU, Memory, Device, and Topology managers that consume container manager hints\n- **Cgroup Drivers**: Both cgroupv1 and cgroupv2 implementations for enforcing limits\n- **Internal Container Lifecycle**: Hooks that run before/after container creation\n\n**Related Subsystems:**\n- **Cgroup Management** (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_*.go`): Abstracts cgroup v1/v2 differences\n- **QoS Management** (`pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_*.go`): Manages QoS class hierarchy\n- **Pod Status Provider** (`pkg/kubelet/status/`): Reports container resource status\n- **Plugin Manager** (`pkg/kubelet/pluginmanager/`): Device plugin registration and lifecycle\n\n## Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### Core Container Manager Interface (`container_manager.go`)\n\nThe `ContainerManager` interface defines the contract for resource management:\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go:66-170\n```\n\n**Primary Responsibilities:**\n\n1. **Initialization and Lifecycle**\n   - `Start()`: Initializes all resource managers, validates system requirements, sets up QoS cgroup hierarchy\n   - `GetNodeConfig()`: Returns configuration including cgroup driver, policies, and resource reservations\n\n2. **Cgroup Management**\n   - `GetMountedSubsystems()`: Returns mounted cgroup subsystems on the node\n   - `GetPodCgroupRoot()`: Returns the root cgroup path for all pods\n   - `GetQOSContainersInfo()`: Provides names of Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort cgroup containers\n   - `UpdateQOSCgroups()`: Synchronizes QoS container state periodically\n\n3. **Resource Allocation**\n   - `GetResources()`: Prepares RunContainerOptions with devices, mounts, and environment variables\n   - `GetCapacity()`: Returns node's total allocatable resources\n   - `GetNodeAllocatableReservation()`: Returns system and kubelet reserved amounts\n   - `GetDevicePluginResourceCapacity()`: Returns device plugin resource accounting\n\n4. **Pod Resource Management**\n   - `NewPodContainerManager()`: Creates pod-level container manager for QoS enforcement\n   - `PrepareDynamicResources()`: Allocates DRA resources before pod starts\n   - `UnprepareDynamicResources()`: Cleans up DRA resources after pod stops\n\n5. **Extension and Monitoring**\n   - `GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()`: Allows device plugins to register\n   - `GetHealthCheckers()`: Provides health checks for monitoring\n   - `InternalContainerLifecycle()`: Returns lifecycle hooks for pre/post container operations\n   - `Updates()`: Channel receiving resource update notifications\n\n### Linux Container Manager Implementation (`container_manager_linux.go`)\n\nThe concrete implementation instantiates and coordinates all resource managers.\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:100-140\n```\n\n**Key Fields:**\n- `cgroupManager`: Handles cgroup creation/update (abstracts v1 vs v2)\n- `qosContainerManager`: Manages QoS class cgroup hierarchy\n- `topologyManager`: Coordinates NUMA-aware resource allocation\n- `cpuManager`: Allocates exclusive CPUs or shares\n- `memoryManager`: Manages memory allocation and reserved memory\n- `deviceManager`: Tracks device plugin resources\n- `draManager`: Manages Dynamic Resource Allocation framework\n- `capacity` and `internalCapacity`: Node resource accounting\n- `systemContainers`: System processes that need resource protection\n\n**Initialization Sequence** (lines 207-391):\n1. Detects cgroup subsystems and cgroup version (v1 vs v2)\n2. Detects swap enablement (fails if swap on and not allowed)\n3. Queries cAdvisor for machine info and capacity\n4. Creates cgroup manager (selecting v1 or v2 driver)\n5. Validates node allocatable cgroup-root exists\n6. Creates QoS container manager for hierarchy\n7. Initializes topology manager with machine topology\n8. Initializes device manager with topology awareness\n9. Initializes CPU manager with selected policy (none/static)\n10. Initializes memory manager with selected policy (none/static)\n11. Creates resource update channel and fan-in goroutines\n\n**Setup Sequence** (called during Start, lines 504-584):\n1. Validates system requirements (required cgroups mounted)\n2. Validates kernel tunable flags (OOM panic, swappiness)\n3. Creates node allocatable cgroup if enabled\n4. Starts QoS container manager\n5. Enforces node allocatable limits\n6. Creates system containers (kubelet, system services)\n7. Spawns periodic task goroutines\n\n### Resource Managers\n\n#### CPU Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Allocates CPUs to containers with choice of two policies:\n- **None Policy**: All CPUs shared, no exclusive allocation\n- **Static Policy**: Pins whole CPUs to containers requesting integer CPU requests\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go:56-102\n```\n\n**Key Operations:**\n- `Allocate()`: Called during pod admission to reserve CPUs\n- `AddContainer()`: Called after container starts (maps container ID to allocation)\n- `RemoveContainer()`: Called when container stops (frees CPUs)\n- `GetTopologyHints()`: Provides NUMA hints to topology manager\n- `GetExclusiveCPUs()`: Returns pinned CPUs for a container\n\n**State Management**:\n- Checkpoints allocation state to disk (`cpu_manager_state` file in kubelet root dir)\n- Reconciliation loop periodically compares checkpoint vs runtime state\n- Updates container CPU CFS quota/period through CRI if changed\n\n#### Memory Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Manages memory affinity and reservation for NUMA systems:\n- **None Policy**: No memory pinning, uses system defaults\n- **Static Policy**: Pins memory allocations to specific NUMA nodes\n\n**Key Operations:**\n- Same lifecycle as CPU manager (Allocate, AddContainer, RemoveContainer)\n- `GetTopologyHints()`: Provides memory NUMA affinity hints\n- Checkpoints and reconciles memory allocations\n\n#### Topology Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Coordinates topology-aware resource allocation across all hint providers.\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go:58-96\n```\n\n**Design Pattern - HintProvider Interface**:\n```\nGetTopologyHints(pod, container) -> map[resourceName][]TopologyHint\nGetPodTopologyHints(pod) -> map[resourceName][]TopologyHint\nAllocate(pod, container) -> error\n```\n\n**Policy Options**:\n- **None**: No topology awareness\n- **BestEffort**: Returns preferred hints but doesn't reject if unavailable\n- **Restricted**: Rejects pod if preferred topology not available\n- **SingleNumaNode**: Requires all resources on single NUMA node\n\n**Scope Options**:\n- **Container**: Makes topology decisions per container\n- **Pod**: Makes topology decisions for entire pod at once\n\n**Flow for Pod Admission**:\n1. Topology manager asks all hint providers for topology hints\n2. Merges hints from CPU, Memory, Device managers\n3. Selects best hint according to policy\n4. Calls Allocate on each provider with selected affinity\n5. Providers then actually reserve resources on selected NUMA nodes\n\n#### Device Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Manages device plugins and allocates custom resources.\n\n**Plugin Architecture**:\n- Watches for device plugin socket registration in `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/`\n- Connects to device plugins via gRPC\n- Calls plugin's `Allocate()` RPC when pod needs device resources\n- Returns mount points, environment variables, and device IDs to container\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `GetResources()`: Returns RunContainerOptions for device allocation\n- `GetTopologyHints()`: Provides topology hints for device NUMA locality\n- `UpdatePluginResources()`: Updates node allocatable after plugin health changes\n\n#### DRA Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Implements Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) framework for custom resources.\n\n**Lifecycle**:\n- `PrepareDynamicResources()`: Calls DRA driver to allocate resources before pod starts\n- `UnprepareDynamicResources()`: Calls DRA driver to deallocate resources when pod stops\n- Manages resourceclaim bindings and driver communication\n\n### Cgroup Management Layer (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_*.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Abstracts cgroup v1 and v2 differences with unified interface.\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go:62-97\n```\n\n**CgroupManager Interface**:\n- `Create()`: Creates cgroup with ResourceConfig\n- `Update()`: Updates cgroup resource limits\n- `Destroy()`: Removes cgroup\n- `Validate()`: Checks cgroup validity\n- `MemoryUsage()`: Reads current memory usage\n- `Pids()`: Lists processes in cgroup\n\n**Implementations**:\n- **cgroupV1Manager** (`cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`): Uses legacy cgroup v1 subsystems (cpu, memory, cpuset, etc.)\n- **cgroupV2Manager** (`cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`): Uses unified cgroup v2 interface\n\n**Resource Parameters** (lines 27-44):\n- Memory limit\n- CPU share weight (cpu.shares)\n- CPU quota/period (cpu.cfs_quota_us, cpu.cfs_period_us)\n- CPUSet (cpuset.cpus)\n- HugePage limits\n- Process ID limits\n- cgroup v2 unified parameters\n\n### QoS Container Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_*.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Maintains QoS class cgroup hierarchy and enforces quality of service.\n\n**Cgroup Hierarchy**:\n```\nroot\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 kubepods           (kubeReserved)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 guaranteed     (no limit)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 burstable      (pod request limit)\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 besteffort     (pod request limit, eviction priority)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 system.slice       (systemReserved)\n```\n\n**Operations**:\n- `Start()`: Creates initial QoS cgroup hierarchy\n- `UpdateCgroups()`: Applies current resource limits to QoS containers\n- Called by container manager during Start and periodically\n\n### Pod Container Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_*.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Creates and manages pod-level cgroups when QoS hierarchy enabled.\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go:106-141\n```\n\n**Operations**:\n- `EnsureExists()`: Creates pod cgroup with appropriate QoS limit\n- `Destroy()`: Removes pod cgroup when pod terminates\n- `GetPodContainerName()`: Maps pod to its cgroup name\n- `GetAllPodsFromCgroups()`: Enumerates pods from cgroupfs for reconciliation\n\n**Pod Cgroup Path**:\n```\nkubepods/[qos-class]/pod-[pod-uid]/\n```\n\nPod containers are placed under this cgroup, with resource limits based on pod QoS class.\n\n### Internal Container Lifecycle (`internal_container_lifecycle.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Runs pre/post container hooks from resource managers.\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go:28-57\n```\n\n**Hooks Called**:\n- `PreCreateContainer()`: Before CRI CreateContainer RPC (unused currently)\n- `PreStartContainer()`: After container created, before start\n  - CPU manager adds container to its tracking\n  - Memory manager adds container to its tracking\n  - Topology manager records container in its store\n- `PostStopContainer()`: After container stops\n  - Topology manager removes container from store\n  - Note: CPU/Memory removal happens through RemoveContainer RPC\n\n## End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 1. Container Manager Initialization (lines 615-621 and 504-584)\n\n**Trigger**: Kubelet Start() during node boot\n\n**Flow**:\n```\nkubelet.Start()\n  \u2193\ncontainerManager.Start(ctx, node, activePods, ...)\n  \u2193\n1. Build container runtime map from current containers\n  \u2193\n2. Start resource managers (DRA, CPU, Memory)\n  \u2193\n3. setupNode():\n   - Validate kernel tunables\n   - Create node allocatable cgroups\n   - Start QoS container manager\n   - Enforce node allocatable limits\n   - Create system containers\n  \u2193\n4. Spawn periodic maintenance goroutines\n  \u2193\n5. Return ready for pod operations\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- Init: `NewContainerManager()` lines 207-391\n- Setup: `setupNode()` lines 504-584\n- Start goroutines: lines 672-704\n\n### 2. Pod Admission with Resource Allocation\n\n**Trigger**: Pod arrives at kubelet, before container creation\n\n**Flow**:\n```\nadmissionHandler.Admit(pod)\n  \u2193\n1. Call containerManager.UpdatePluginResources()\n   - Device plugins update their allocatable\n  \u2193\n2. For DRA resources: PrepareDynamicResources()\n   - DRA manager allocates claims\n  \u2193\n3. For each container: containerManager.GetResources()\n   - Gathers CPU/Memory/Device allocation\n   - Returns mounts, environment, devices\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- GetResources: container_manager_linux.go lines 727-800\n- Device allocation: devicemanager/manager.go\n- DRA preparation: dra/manager.go\n\n### 3. Container Resource Enforcement During Creation\n\n**Trigger**: After CRI CreateContainer, before StartContainer\n\n**Flow**:\n```\nkuberuntime.runContainer()\n  \u2193\n1. Create container with CRI\n  \u2193\n2. Call internalContainerLifecycle.PreStartContainer()\n   - cpuManager.AddContainer() - track for reconciliation\n   - memoryManager.AddContainer() - track for reconciliation\n   - topologyManager.AddContainer() - record in store\n  \u2193\n3. Start container with CRI\n  \u2193\n4. Container has resource limits enforced via cgroups\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- Internal lifecycle: internal_container_lifecycle.go:41-53\n- CPU tracking: cpumanager/cpu_manager.go AddContainer method\n- Topology tracking: topologymanager/topology_manager.go:65\n\n### 4. CPU Reconciliation Loop (CPU Manager)\n\n**Trigger**: Periodic reconciliation (default ~5 seconds)\n\n**Flow**:\n```\nreconcileState() in CPU manager\n  \u2193\n1. Read checkpoint file (cpu_manager_state)\n  \u2193\n2. Compare with active containers from runtime\n  \u2193\n3. For changed allocations:\n   - Update cgroup CPU CFS quota/period\n   - Call CRI UpdateContainerResources()\n  \u2193\n4. Handle newly created/removed containers\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- CPU reconcile: cpumanager/cpu_manager.go Start() method ~line 275\n\n### 5. Topology-Aware Allocation Decision\n\n**Trigger**: Pod admission with topology manager policy (non-none)\n\n**Flow**:\n```\ntopologyManager.Admit(pod) - PodAdmitHandler\n  \u2193\n1. For each container in pod:\n   - Ask CPU manager: GetTopologyHints()\n   - Ask Memory manager: GetTopologyHints()\n   - Ask Device manager: GetTopologyHints()\n  \u2193\n2. Merge hints with policy (bestEffort/restricted/singleNumaNode)\n  \u2193\n3. Select best hint according to policy\n   - Preferred hints prioritized\n   - Narrower NUMA masks prioritized\n  \u2193\n4. Store affinity in topology manager\n  \u2193\n5. Call Allocate on each hint provider\n   - CPU manager: pins CPUs to NUMA nodes\n   - Memory manager: pins memory to NUMA nodes\n   - Device manager: selects devices from NUMA node\n  \u2193\n6. Return (allow or reject based on policy)\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- Topology manager: topologymanager/topology_manager.go lines 136-198\n- Pod scope: topologymanager/scope_pod.go\n- Container scope: topologymanager/scope_container.go\n\n### 6. QoS Cgroup Hierarchy Update\n\n**Trigger**: Periodically during container lifecycle\n\n**Flow**:\n```\nkubelet.syncNodeStatus() or direct call\n  \u2193\ncontainerManager.UpdateQOSCgroups()\n  \u2193\nqosContainerManager.UpdateCgroups()\n  \u2193\nFor guaranteed, burstable, besteffort:\n  1. Calculate total pod requests in class\n  2. Update cgroup memory.limit_in_bytes\n  3. Update CPU shares proportionally\n  4. Apply cgroup manager Update() calls\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- Update: qos_container_manager_linux.go UpdateCgroups method\n\n### 7. Container Removal\n\n**Trigger**: Pod deletion or container failure\n\n**Flow**:\n```\npodWorker.ManagePodLoop() \u2192 Kubelet removes container\n  \u2193\n1. Call CRI StopContainer/RemoveContainer\n  \u2193\n2. Call internalContainerLifecycle.PostStopContainer()\n   - topologyManager.RemoveContainer()\n  \u2193\n3. Call resource managers' RemoveContainer()\n   - cpuManager.RemoveContainer() - free CPUs\n   - memoryManager.RemoveContainer() - free memory reservation\n  \u2193\n4. Pod container removed when last container gone\n   - podContainerManager.Destroy()\n   - Remove pod cgroup\n  \u2193\n5. On pod deletion: UnprepareDynamicResources()\n   - DRA deallocates claims\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- Pod removal: pod_container_manager_linux.go Destroy method\n\n## Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### System Validation Failures\n\n**Mounted Cgroup Subsystems** (`validateSystemRequirements`, lines 151-202):\n- **Failure**: cpu, cpuacct, cpuset, memory subsystems not mounted\n- **Impact**: Container manager won't initialize\n- **Mitigation**: Check cgroup mounts before kubelet startup\n\n**CPU CFS Quota** (`validateSystemRequirements`, lines 188-200):\n- **Failure**: cpu.cfs_quota_us or cpu.cfs_period_us not available\n- **Impact**: Set as \"soft requirement\" in status, container manager continues\n- **Concern**: Cannot enforce CPU limits accurately\n- **Tradeoff**: Allows operation in cgroup v2 where CFS quota works differently\n\n**Kernel Tunables** (`setupKernelTunables`, lines 456-502):\n- **Parameters**: VM overcommit memory, panic on OOM, kernel panic settings\n- **Failure Modes**:\n  - `ProtectKernelDefaults=true`: Fails if any tunable differs (production safety)\n  - Default: Warns but continues (allows flexibility in test environments)\n- **Tradeoff**: Production deployments must match expectations\n\n### Resource Allocation Failures\n\n**Topology Affinity Errors**:\n- **Policy=Restricted**: Rejects pod if preferred topology unavailable\n- **Policy=BestEffort**: Accepts pod with suboptimal affinity\n- **Tradeoff**: Restricted is stricter but may reject valid workloads; BestEffort is more lenient but may cause performance degradation\n\n**CPU Static Policy Constraints**:\n- Requires nonzero CPU reservation (no shared pool exhaustion)\n- Cannot allocate fractional CPUs exclusively\n- Only supports integer CPU requests for pinning\n- **Tradeoff**: Simplicity vs. fine-grained control\n\n**Memory Static Policy Constraints**:\n- Requires reserved memory specification\n- Cannot dynamically adjust memory affinity after allocation\n- **Tradeoff**: Predictability vs. flexibility\n\n### Device Plugin Failures\n\n**Plugin Registration Timeout**:\n- Device plugins must register within startup window\n- If plugin absent: Resource unavailable to pods\n- If plugin fails: Devices become unhealthy, pods rejected\n\n**Device Allocation Failure**:\n- If plugin's Allocate() RPC fails: Container creation fails\n- Pod stays in pending state until resolved\n\n**Health Monitoring**:\n- Device manager periodically checks plugin health\n- Unhealthy plugins' resources removed from allocatable\n\n### Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) Failures\n\n**Resource Claim Allocation**:\n- DRA driver must allocate claim before pod starts\n- If allocation fails: Pod rejected at admission\n- Claim remains in allocated state for retry\n\n**Pre-allocation Timeout**:\n- PrepareDynamicResources must complete before pod moves to running\n- Long-running allocations may delay pod startup\n\n### QoS Hierarchy Edge Cases\n\n**Pod in Multiple QoS Classes**:\n- Mixed request/limit across containers determines class\n- At least one container determines pod class\n- **Tradeoff**: Simplicity; cannot mix QoS in one pod\n\n**Node Allocatable Enforcement**:\n- Pods placed under node allocatable cgroup limit\n- System services protected by separate hierarchy\n- **Concern**: If system services exceed reservation, cannot be killed\n- **Mitigation**: System reserved sizing must match actual usage\n\n### Limit Enforcement Levels\n\n**Hard Limits** (enforced immediately):\n- Memory.limit_in_bytes: OOM killer invoked if exceeded\n- cpu.cfs_quota_us: Hard CPU cap (some variance in enforcement)\n- device limits: Devices unavailable if exhausted\n\n**Soft Limits** (advisory):\n- cpu.shares: CPU weight, only enforced under contention\n- memory.soft_limit_in_bytes: Reclaimed under pressure, but memory not freed\n\n**Unrecognized Requests**:\n- Device plugins: Unknown devices silently ignored if not requested\n- Memory nodes: Requests beyond available nodes may pin to available subset\n\n### Scale Limitations\n\n**Maximum NUMA Nodes**: 8 nodes (hardcoded in topology manager, line 41 of topology_manager.go)\n- **Rationale**: Hint enumeration explodes combinatorially with NUMA nodes\n- **Impact**: Cannot enable topology manager on 16+ NUMA node systems\n\n**Container Count**:\n- Reconciliation loops iterate all active containers\n- No known hard limit, but performance degrades O(n) with containers\n\n**Device Plugin Count**:\n- Device manager maintains list of plugins\n- Each plugin connection is a goroutine\n- No hard limit, but resource usage grows with plugins\n\n## Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 1. Container Manager Policies\n\n**CPU Manager Policies** (pluggable via `--cpu-manager-policy`):\n- `none`: No management, all CPUs shared\n- `static`: Exclusive CPU pinning for integer requests\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- New policies must implement reconciliation and checkpoint logic\n- Incorrect reconciliation can cause CPU leaks or over-allocation\n- No runtime policy switching (requires restart)\n\n**Memory Manager Policies** (pluggable via `--memory-manager-policy`):\n- `none`: No management\n- `static`: NUMA node pinning\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Memory cannot be repurposed easily like CPUs\n- Failed deallocation leaves memory pinned indefinitely\n\n### 2. Topology Manager Policies\n\n**Policies** (pluggable via `--topology-manager-policy`):\n- `none`: No topology awareness\n- `best-effort`: Returns hints but doesn't reject\n- `restricted`: Rejects if preferred hint unavailable\n- `single-numa-node`: Requires single NUMA node\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Custom policies must merge hints correctly\n- Incorrect merging can allow conflicting allocations\n- Policy changes require node draining (affects all pods)\n\n### 3. Topology Manager Scopes\n\n**Scopes** (pluggable via `--topology-manager-scope`):\n- `container`: Per-container topology decisions\n- `pod`: Pod-wide topology decisions\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Scope changes affect how hints are gathered and merged\n- Changing scope requires pod restart to take effect\n\n### 4. Device Plugin Interface\n\n**Standard Plugin Registration** (Unix socket in `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/`):\n\n**Plugin Hooks**:\n- `GetDevicePluginOptions()`: Declare PreStartRequired, GetPreferredAllocationAvailable\n- `ListAndWatch()`: Stream device updates\n- `Allocate()`: Called before container starts\n- `PreStartContainer()`: Optional, called before container actually starts\n- `GetPreferredAllocation()`: Optional, called before Allocate to prefer certain devices\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Buggy plugins can hang kubelet if synchronous calls timeout\n- Plugins crashing leave processes orphaned\n- Malicious plugin could exhaust system resources\n- PreStartContainer hook runs with elevated privileges (can modify container)\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Plugin server timeout prevents indefinite hangs\n- Health checks periodically restart plugins\n- Plugin resource usage not limited (trust model)\n\n### 5. Cgroup Driver Selection\n\n**Cgroup Drivers** (pluggable via `--cgroup-driver`):\n- `cgroupfs`: Direct filesystem manipulation\n- `systemd`: Uses systemd slice/scope units\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Wrong driver selection incompatible with system\n- Mixing drivers on same node causes conflicts\n- cgroupfs has some privilege escalation vectors if misconfigured\n\n**Platform Variance**:\n- systemd driver only available on systemd systems (most modern Linux)\n- cgroupfs works on any cgroup v1 system\n- cgroup v2 unified interface works differently for both drivers\n\n### 6. QoS and Node Allocatable Customization\n\n**Node Allocatable Configuration** (via `--system-reserved`, `--kube-reserved`, `--eviction-hard`):\n- Controls how much resources reserved from pods\n- Incorrect sizing can starve system services\n- Over-reservation leaves unused capacity\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Changing reservation requires node restart\n- System services exceeding reservation cannot be evicted\n- No enforcement of actual usage vs. reservation\n\n### 7. Pod Admission Handler\n\n**PodAdmitHandler Interface** (for container manager, topology manager):\n- Called before pod enters the node\n- Can reject pod if resources unavailable\n- Runs serially for all pods being admitted\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Slow admission handlers block scheduler\n- Rejecting pods with invalid reason confuses scheduler\n- Cannot access pod's actual runtime requirements\n\n### 8. Plugin Registration Handler\n\n**PluginHandler Interface** (for device manager):\n- Called when plugin socket appears/disappears\n- Manages plugin connection lifecycle\n- Runs concurrently across plugins\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Plugin directory has relaxed permissions (`/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/`)\n- Malicious code can create fake plugin socket\n- Plugin can be injected at runtime (root access required, but possible)\n\n## Operational Implications\n\n### Performance Characteristics\n\n**CPU Overhead**:\n1. **Topology Manager**: Generates hints for all resources (O(number of providers \u00d7 containers))\n   - Linear in container count, exponential in NUMA nodes\n   - Evaluation happens at pod admission (synchronous, affects scheduler latency)\n\n2. **CPU Manager Reconciliation**: O(active containers) every ~5 seconds\n   - Updates only changed containers (incremental)\n   - CRI call per changed container (batching not possible)\n\n3. **Memory Manager**: Similar to CPU manager in reconciliation cost\n\n4. **QoS Update**: O(pods) to update cgroup limits\n   - Runs periodically, not per-container change\n   - Scales poorly with high pod churn\n\n**Memory Overhead**:\n- Topology manager caches hints per provider \u00d7 container (O(containers \u00d7 providers \u00d7 NUMA nodes))\n- CPU/Memory managers checkpoint to disk (small files, ~1KB per container)\n- Device manager maps all plugin devices in memory (O(devices across all plugins))\n\n### Reliability and Monitoring\n\n**Health Checks**:\n- Device manager monitors plugin health (periodic List/Watch)\n- Unhealthy plugins' resources marked unavailable\n- No automatic plugin restart (external mechanism required)\n\n**Observability**:\n- Topology manager emits `TopologyAffinityError` when pod cannot be admitted\n- Device manager logs allocation failures\n- CPU/Memory manager logs reconciliation mismatches\n- Container manager logs setup failures\n\n**Checkpointing**:\n- CPU manager checkpoints state on every Allocate/RemoveContainer\n- Memory manager checkpoints state on every Allocate/RemoveContainer\n- Checkpoint loss on kubelet restart means lost allocations (pods must be recreated)\n- Stale checkpoint can block pod from scheduling if not cleaned\n\n### Scalability Considerations\n\n**Node Density**:\n- Topology manager scales poorly beyond 100 pods with topology policies enabled\n- Hint enumeration and merging becomes bottleneck\n- Recommendation: Use `topology-manager-policy: none` for high-density nodes\n\n**Large Pod Count**:\n- QoS cgroup updates are O(pods), running periodically\n- Device allocation calls are per-pod, not batched\n- Recommendation: Monitor resource manager reconciliation latency\n\n**Device Plugins**:\n- Each plugin requires dedicated socket and connection\n- Plugins consuming large memory or CPU should be monitored separately\n- Recommend: Consolidate multiple devices into single plugin\n\n### Node Upgrades and Changes\n\n**Cgroup Version Migration** (v1 to v2):\n- Requires node drain and kubelet restart\n- Cannot change `--cgroup-driver` without drain\n- Recommendation: Migrate during maintenance window with pod eviction\n\n**Topology Manager Policy Changes**:\n- Policy changes (e.g., `none` \u2192 `restricted`) affect all pods\n- Pods with non-preferred topology may be rejected\n- Recommendation: Apply during maintenance window, monitor pod failures\n\n**Device Plugin Lifecycle**:\n- Plugins can be installed/removed without node restart\n- New plugin appears in device list after registration\n- Recommendation: Drain nodes before removing plugins\n\n**System Reserved Changes**:\n- `--system-reserved` changes require node restart\n- Over-reservation may strand resources\n- Under-reservation may crash system services\n- Recommendation: Size based on actual system usage, not estimates\n\n### Failure Recovery\n\n**Stuck Pods (Resource Allocation)**:\n- If DRA allocation fails: Pod stays pending indefinitely\n- If device unavailable: Pod stays pending\n- Recovery: Fix underlying resource issue, pod automatically retries\n\n**Cgroup Cleanup**:\n- Orphaned cgroups remain after container crash\n- Container manager handles cleanup on new pod creation\n- Manual cleanup: `cgdelete` or systemd tools\n\n**Corrupted Checkpoint**:\n- CPU/Memory manager checkpoint corruption causes allocation failures\n- Recovery: Delete checkpoint file (`cpu_manager_state`), restart kubelet\n- Risk: Newly started containers may get same CPUs (collision)\n\n### Backward Compatibility\n\n**Policy Changes**:\n- CPU policy switch (none \u2194 static) requires kubelet restart\n- Changing mid-flight could cause allocation conflicts\n- No migration path: Manual pod recreation required\n\n**Cgroup Driver Switch**:\n- Requires node drain, cgroup migration, kubelet restart\n- Existing cgroup hierarchies incompatible between drivers\n- High-risk operation\n\n**QoS Hierarchy Changes**:\n- Enabling `--cgroups-per-qos` on existing node requires pod eviction\n- No automatic migration of existing pods to QoS cgroups\n\n## Map of Important Files and Directories\n\n```\npkg/kubelet/cm/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 container_manager.go                 # Core ContainerManager interface (66-170)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 container_manager_linux.go           # Linux implementation (100-700+)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 container_manager_windows.go         # Windows implementation\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 container_manager_stub.go            # No-op implementation (for unsupported systems)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 types.go                             # CgroupManager, PodContainerManager interfaces\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 internal_container_lifecycle.go      # PreStart/PostStop container hooks (28-57)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 cgroup_manager_linux.go              # Cgroup abstraction layer (40-150+)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go           # cgroup v1 implementation\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go           # cgroup v2 implementation\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 cgroup_manager_unsupported.go        # No-op for non-Linux\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 qos_container_manager_linux.go       # QoS class cgroup hierarchy\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 pod_container_manager_linux.go       # Pod-level cgroup management\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 cpumanager/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpu_manager.go                   # CPU allocation manager (56-102)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 policy.go                        # CPU policy interface\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 policy_none.go                   # None policy (shared CPUs)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 policy_static.go                 # Static policy (exclusive CPUs)\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 state/                           # CPU state checkpoint\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 memorymanager/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 memory_manager.go topologymanager/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 topology_manager.go              # Topology coordination (58-96)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 policy.go                        # Topology policy interface\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 policy_best_effort.go            # Best effort topology\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 policy_restricted.go             # Restricted topology\n\u2502 scope_container.go               # Per-container scope\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 scope_pod.go                     # Per-pod scope\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 bitmask/                         #         \u251c\u2500\u2500 client.go                # Device plugin gRPC client\n\u2502           \u251c\u2500\u2500 server.go                # Device plugin gRPC server\n\u2502 provider\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 cadvisor/                            # Machine info and capacity\n```\n\n## Summary\n\nThe kubelet container manager is a sophisticated resource coordination system that:\n\n1. **Layers abstractions** from system cgroups up to Kubernetes QoS classes\n2. **Coordinates multiple managers** (CPU, Memory, Device, Topology) via hint-based negotiation\n3. **Maintains checkpoints** to survive kubelet restarts without losing allocations\n4. **Provides extension points** (policies, plugins, drivers) with clear security boundaries\n5. **Balances flexibility with predictability** through policy selection at node configuration time\n\nSuccess depends on correct sizing of system reserved resources, appropriate policy selection for workload characteristics, and understanding the tradeoffs between strict affinity requirements vs. flexible resource allocation.\n\n",

{
  "content": "# Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nThe kubelet container manager subsystem is responsible for managing container resources, enforcing Quality of Service (QoS) classes, and coordinating resource allocation across CPU, memory, and device plugins. It sits at the intersection of pod scheduling, container runtime execution, and system resource enforcement on the node.\n\nThe container manager operates at several levels:\n- **System level**: Managing system containers and daemon processes\n- **Node level**: Enforcing node allocatable reservations and capacity limits\n- **Pod level**: Creating pod cgroups and managing QoS hierarchies\n- **Container level**: Allocating exclusive resources and updating runtime constraints\n\n## Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\nThe container manager ensures that:\n1. Container resource requests and limits are enforced through cgroup mechanisms\n2. Resources are allocated according to pod QoS classes (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort)\n3. Topology-aware resource allocation is coordinated across multiple resource managers\n4. Device plugins can register and provide custom resources\n5. Dynamic resource allocation can be managed through DRA framework\n6. System services and kubelet process have protected resource reservations\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies:**\n- **Kubelet Core** (`pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go`): Initializes the container manager during startup and calls it for pod admission and container lifecycle hooks\n- **Pod Workers** (`pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`): Request container lifecycle operations through the manager\n- **Runtime Service** (CRI): Container manager updates container resources through CRI calls to adjust CPU/memory constraints\n- **cAdvisor** (`pkg/kubelet/cadvisor/`): Provides machine topology and filesystem capacity information\n\n**Downstream Dependents:**\n- **Pod Container Manager** (`pkg/kubelet/cm/`): Manages pod-level cgroups based on QoS class\n- **Resource Managers**: CPU, Memory, Device, and Topology managers that consume container manager hints\n- **Cgroup Drivers**: Both cgroupv1 and cgroupv2 implementations for enforcing limits\n- **Internal Container Lifecycle**: Hooks that run before/after container creation\n\n**Related Subsystems:**\n- **Cgroup Management** (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_*.go`): Abstracts cgroup v1/v2 differences\n- **QoS Management** (`pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_*.go`): Manages QoS class hierarchy\n- **Pod Status Provider** (`pkg/kubelet/status/`): Reports container resource status\n- **Plugin Manager** (`pkg/kubelet/pluginmanager/`): Device plugin registration and lifecycle\n\n## Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### Core Container Manager Interface (`container_manager.go`)\n\nThe `ContainerManager` interface defines the contract for resource management:\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go:66-170\n```\n\n**Primary Responsibilities:**\n\n1. **Initialization and Lifecycle**\n   - `Start()`: Initializes all resource managers, validates system requirements, sets up QoS cgroup hierarchy\n   - `GetNodeConfig()`: Returns configuration including cgroup driver, policies, and resource reservations\n\n2. **Cgroup Management**\n   - `GetMountedSubsystems()`: Returns mounted cgroup subsystems on the node\n   - `GetPodCgroupRoot()`: Returns the root cgroup path for all pods\n   - `GetQOSContainersInfo()`: Provides names of Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort cgroup containers\n   - `UpdateQOSCgroups()`: Synchronizes QoS container state periodically\n\n3. **Resource Allocation**\n   - `GetResources()`: Prepares RunContainerOptions with devices, mounts, and environment variables\n   - `GetCapacity()`: Returns node's total allocatable resources\n   - `GetNodeAllocatableReservation()`: Returns system and kubelet reserved amounts\n   - `GetDevicePluginResourceCapacity()`: Returns device plugin resource accounting\n\n4. **Pod Resource Management**\n   - `NewPodContainerManager()`: Creates pod-level container manager for QoS enforcement\n   - `PrepareDynamicResources()`: Allocates DRA resources before pod starts\n   - `UnprepareDynamicResources()`: Cleans up DRA resources after pod stops\n\n5. **Extension and Monitoring**\n   - `GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()`: Allows device plugins to register\n   - `GetHealthCheckers()`: Provides health checks for monitoring\n   - `InternalContainerLifecycle()`: Returns lifecycle hooks for pre/post container operations\n   - `Updates()`: Channel receiving resource update notifications\n\n### Linux Container Manager Implementation (`container_manager_linux.go`)\n\nThe concrete implementation instantiates and coordinates all resource managers.\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:100-140\n```\n\n**Key Fields:**\n- `cgroupManager`: Handles cgroup creation/update (abstracts v1 vs v2)\n- `qosContainerManager`: Manages QoS class cgroup hierarchy\n- `topologyManager`: Coordinates NUMA-aware resource allocation\n- `cpuManager`: Allocates exclusive CPUs or shares\n- `memoryManager`: Manages memory allocation and reserved memory\n- `deviceManager`: Tracks device plugin resources\n- `draManager`: Manages Dynamic Resource Allocation framework\n- `capacity` and `internalCapacity`: Node resource accounting\n- `systemContainers`: System processes that need resource protection\n\n**Initialization Sequence** (lines 207-391):\n1. Detects cgroup subsystems and cgroup version (v1 vs v2)\n2. Detects swap enablement (fails if swap on and not allowed)\n3. Queries cAdvisor for machine info and capacity\n4. Creates cgroup manager (selecting v1 or v2 driver)\n5. Validates node allocatable cgroup-root exists\n6. Creates QoS container manager for hierarchy\n7. Initializes topology manager with machine topology\n8. Initializes device manager with topology awareness\n9. Initializes CPU manager with selected policy (none/static)\n10. Initializes memory manager with selected policy (none/static)\n11. Creates resource update channel and fan-in goroutines\n\n**Setup Sequence** (called during Start, lines 504-584):\n1. Validates system requirements (required cgroups mounted)\n2. Validates kernel tunable flags (OOM panic, swappiness)\n3. Creates node allocatable cgroup if enabled\n4. Starts QoS container manager\n5. Enforces node allocatable limits\n6. Creates system containers (kubelet, system services)\n7. Spawns periodic task goroutines\n\n### Resource Managers\n\n#### CPU Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Allocates CPUs to containers with choice of two policies:\n- **None Policy**: All CPUs shared, no exclusive allocation\n- **Static Policy**: Pins whole CPUs to containers requesting integer CPU requests\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go:56-102\n```\n\n**Key Operations:**\n- `Allocate()`: Called during pod admission to reserve CPUs\n- `AddContainer()`: Called after container starts (maps container ID to allocation)\n- `RemoveContainer()`: Called when container stops (frees CPUs)\n- `GetTopologyHints()`: Provides NUMA hints to topology manager\n- `GetExclusiveCPUs()`: Returns pinned CPUs for a container\n\n**State Management**:\n- Checkpoints allocation state to disk (`cpu_manager_state` file in kubelet root dir)\n- Reconciliation loop periodically compares checkpoint vs runtime state\n- Updates container CPU CFS quota/period through CRI if changed\n\n#### Memory Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Manages memory affinity and reservation for NUMA systems:\n- **None Policy**: No memory pinning, uses system defaults\n- **Static Policy**: Pins memory allocations to specific NUMA nodes\n\n**Key Operations:**\n- Same lifecycle as CPU manager (Allocate, AddContainer, RemoveContainer)\n- `GetTopologyHints()`: Provides memory NUMA affinity hints\n- Checkpoints and reconciles memory allocations\n\n#### Topology Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Coordinates topology-aware resource allocation across all hint providers.\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go:58-96\n```\n\n**Design Pattern - HintProvider Interface**:\n```\nGetTopologyHints(pod, container) -> map[resourceName][]TopologyHint\nGetPodTopologyHints(pod) -> map[resourceName][]TopologyHint\nAllocate(pod, container) -> error\n```\n\n**Policy Options**:\n- **None**: No topology awareness\n- **BestEffort**: Returns preferred hints but doesn't reject if unavailable\n- **Restricted**: Rejects pod if preferred topology not available\n- **SingleNumaNode**: Requires all resources on single NUMA node\n\n**Scope Options**:\n- **Container**: Makes topology decisions per container\n- **Pod**: Makes topology decisions for entire pod at once\n\n**Flow for Pod Admission**:\n1. Topology manager asks all hint providers for topology hints\n2. Merges hints from CPU, Memory, Device managers\n3. Selects best hint according to policy\n4. Calls Allocate on each provider with selected affinity\n5. Providers then actually reserve resources on selected NUMA nodes\n\n#### Device Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Manages device plugins and allocates custom resources.\n\n**Plugin Architecture**:\n- Watches for device plugin socket registration in `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/`\n- Connects to device plugins via gRPC\n- Calls plugin's `Allocate()` RPC when pod needs device resources\n- Returns mount points, environment variables, and device IDs to container\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `GetResources()`: Returns RunContainerOptions for device allocation\n- `GetTopologyHints()`: Provides topology hints for device NUMA locality\n- `UpdatePluginResources()`: Updates node allocatable after plugin health changes\n\n#### DRA Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/manager.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Implements Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) framework for custom resources.\n\n**Lifecycle**:\n- `PrepareDynamicResources()`: Calls DRA driver to allocate resources before pod starts\n- `UnprepareDynamicResources()`: Calls DRA driver to deallocate resources when pod stops\n- Manages resourceclaim bindings and driver communication\n\n### Cgroup Management Layer (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_*.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Abstracts cgroup v1 and v2 differences with unified interface.\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go:62-97\n```\n\n**CgroupManager Interface**:\n- `Create()`: Creates cgroup with ResourceConfig\n- `Update()`: Updates cgroup resource limits\n- `Destroy()`: Removes cgroup\n- `Validate()`: Checks cgroup validity\n- `MemoryUsage()`: Reads current memory usage\n- `Pids()`: Lists processes in cgroup\n\n**Implementations**:\n- **cgroupV1Manager** (`cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`): Uses legacy cgroup v1 subsystems (cpu, memory, cpuset, etc.)\n- **cgroupV2Manager** (`cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`): Uses unified cgroup v2 interface\n\n**Resource Parameters** (lines 27-44):\n- Memory limit\n- CPU share weight (cpu.shares)\n- CPU quota/period (cpu.cfs_quota_us, cpu.cfs_period_us)\n- CPUSet (cpuset.cpus)\n- HugePage limits\n- Process ID limits\n- cgroup v2 unified parameters\n\n### QoS Container Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_*.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Maintains QoS class cgroup hierarchy and enforces quality of service.\n\n**Cgroup Hierarchy**:\n```\nroot\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 kubepods           (kubeReserved)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 guaranteed     (no limit)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 burstable      (pod request limit)\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 besteffort     (pod request limit, eviction priority)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 system.slice       (systemReserved)\n```\n\n**Operations**:\n- `Start()`: Creates initial QoS cgroup hierarchy\n- `UpdateCgroups()`: Applies current resource limits to QoS containers\n- Called by container manager during Start and periodically\n\n### Pod Container Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_*.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Creates and manages pod-level cgroups when QoS hierarchy enabled.\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go:106-141\n```\n\n**Operations**:\n- `EnsureExists()`: Creates pod cgroup with appropriate QoS limit\n- `Destroy()`: Removes pod cgroup when pod terminates\n- `GetPodContainerName()`: Maps pod to its cgroup name\n- `GetAllPodsFromCgroups()`: Enumerates pods from cgroupfs for reconciliation\n\n**Pod Cgroup Path**:\n```\nkubepods/[qos-class]/pod-[pod-uid]/\n```\n\nPod containers are placed under this cgroup, with resource limits based on pod QoS class.\n\n### Internal Container Lifecycle (`internal_container_lifecycle.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Runs pre/post container hooks from resource managers.\n\n```\nLocation: pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go:28-57\n```\n\n**Hooks Called**:\n- `PreCreateContainer()`: Before CRI CreateContainer RPC (unused currently)\n- `PreStartContainer()`: After container created, before start\n  - CPU manager adds container to its tracking\n  - Memory manager adds container to its tracking\n  - Topology manager records container in its store\n- `PostStopContainer()`: After container stops\n  - Topology manager removes container from store\n  - Note: CPU/Memory removal happens through RemoveContainer RPC\n\n## End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 1. Container Manager Initialization (lines 615-621 and 504-584)\n\n**Trigger**: Kubelet Start() during node boot\n\n**Flow**:\n```\nkubelet.Start()\n  \u2193\ncontainerManager.Start(ctx, node, activePods, ...)\n  \u2193\n1. Build container runtime map from current containers\n  \u2193\n2. Start resource managers (DRA, CPU, Memory)\n  \u2193\n3. setupNode():\n   - Validate kernel tunables\n   - Create node allocatable cgroups\n   - Start QoS container manager\n   - Enforce node allocatable limits\n   - Create system containers\n  \u2193\n4. Spawn periodic maintenance goroutines\n  \u2193\n5. Return ready for pod operations\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- Init: `NewContainerManager()` lines 207-391\n- Setup: `setupNode()` lines 504-584\n- Start goroutines: lines 672-704\n\n### 2. Pod Admission with Resource Allocation\n\n**Trigger**: Pod arrives at kubelet, before container creation\n\n**Flow**:\n```\nadmissionHandler.Admit(pod)\n  \u2193\n1. Call containerManager.UpdatePluginResources()\n   - Device plugins update their allocatable\n  \u2193\n2. For DRA resources: PrepareDynamicResources()\n   - DRA manager allocates claims\n  \u2193\n3. For each container: containerManager.GetResources()\n   - Gathers CPU/Memory/Device allocation\n   - Returns mounts, environment, devices\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- GetResources: container_manager_linux.go lines 727-800\n- Device allocation: devicemanager/manager.go\n- DRA preparation: dra/manager.go\n\n### 3. Container Resource Enforcement During Creation\n\n**Trigger**: After CRI CreateContainer, before StartContainer\n\n**Flow**:\n```\nkuberuntime.runContainer()\n  \u2193\n1. Create container with CRI\n  \u2193\n2. Call internalContainerLifecycle.PreStartContainer()\n   - cpuManager.AddContainer() - track for reconciliation\n   - memoryManager.AddContainer() - track for reconciliation\n   - topologyManager.AddContainer() - record in store\n  \u2193\n3. Start container with CRI\n  \u2193\n4. Container has resource limits enforced via cgroups\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- Internal lifecycle: internal_container_lifecycle.go:41-53\n- CPU tracking: cpumanager/cpu_manager.go AddContainer method\n- Topology tracking: topologymanager/topology_manager.go:65\n\n### 4. CPU Reconciliation Loop (CPU Manager)\n\n**Trigger**: Periodic reconciliation (default ~5 seconds)\n\n**Flow**:\n```\nreconcileState() in CPU manager\n  \u2193\n1. Read checkpoint file (cpu_manager_state)\n  \u2193\n2. Compare with active containers from runtime\n  \u2193\n3. For changed allocations:\n   - Update cgroup CPU CFS quota/period\n   - Call CRI UpdateContainerResources()\n  \u2193\n4. Handle newly created/removed containers\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- CPU reconcile: cpumanager/cpu_manager.go Start() method ~line 275\n\n### 5. Topology-Aware Allocation Decision\n\n**Trigger**: Pod admission with topology manager policy (non-none)\n\n**Flow**:\n```\ntopologyManager.Admit(pod) - PodAdmitHandler\n  \u2193\n1. For each container in pod:\n   - Ask CPU manager: GetTopologyHints()\n   - Ask Memory manager: GetTopologyHints()\n   - Ask Device manager: GetTopologyHints()\n  \u2193\n2. Merge hints with policy (bestEffort/restricted/singleNumaNode)\n  \u2193\n3. Select best hint according to policy\n   - Preferred hints prioritized\n   - Narrower NUMA masks prioritized\n  \u2193\n4. Store affinity in topology manager\n  \u2193\n5. Call Allocate on each hint provider\n   - CPU manager: pins CPUs to NUMA nodes\n   - Memory manager: pins memory to NUMA nodes\n   - Device manager: selects devices from NUMA node\n  \u2193\n6. Return (allow or reject based on policy)\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- Topology manager: topologymanager/topology_manager.go lines 136-198\n- Pod scope: topologymanager/scope_pod.go\n- Container scope: topologymanager/scope_container.go\n\n### 6. QoS Cgroup Hierarchy Update\n\n**Trigger**: Periodically during container lifecycle\n\n**Flow**:\n```\nkubelet.syncNodeStatus() or direct call\n  \u2193\ncontainerManager.UpdateQOSCgroups()\n  \u2193\nqosContainerManager.UpdateCgroups()\n  \u2193\nFor guaranteed, burstable, besteffort:\n  1. Calculate total pod requests in class\n  2. Update cgroup memory.limit_in_bytes\n  3. Update CPU shares proportionally\n  4. Apply cgroup manager Update() calls\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- Update: qos_container_manager_linux.go UpdateCgroups method\n\n### 7. Container Removal\n\n**Trigger**: Pod deletion or container failure\n\n**Flow**:\n```\npodWorker.ManagePodLoop() \u2192 Kubelet removes container\n  \u2193\n1. Call CRI StopContainer/RemoveContainer\n  \u2193\n2. Call internalContainerLifecycle.PostStopContainer()\n   - topologyManager.RemoveContainer()\n  \u2193\n3. Call resource managers' RemoveContainer()\n   - cpuManager.RemoveContainer() - free CPUs\n   - memoryManager.RemoveContainer() - free memory reservation\n  \u2193\n4. Pod container removed when last container gone\n   - podContainerManager.Destroy()\n   - Remove pod cgroup\n  \u2193\n5. On pod deletion: UnprepareDynamicResources()\n   - DRA deallocates claims\n```\n\n**Critical Code**:\n- Pod removal: pod_container_manager_linux.go Destroy method\n\n## Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### System Validation Failures\n\n**Mounted Cgroup Subsystems** (`validateSystemRequirements`, lines 151-202):\n- **Failure**: cpu, cpuacct, cpuset, memory subsystems not mounted\n- **Impact**: Container manager won't initialize\n- **Mitigation**: Check cgroup mounts before kubelet startup\n\n**CPU CFS Quota** (`validateSystemRequirements`, lines 188-200):\n- **Failure**: cpu.cfs_quota_us or cpu.cfs_period_us not available\n- **Impact**: Set as \"soft requirement\" in status, container manager continues\n- **Concern**: Cannot enforce CPU limits accurately\n- **Tradeoff**: Allows operation in cgroup v2 where CFS quota works differently\n\n**Kernel Tunables** (`setupKernelTunables`, lines 456-502):\n- **Parameters**: VM overcommit memory, panic on OOM, kernel panic settings\n- **Failure Modes**:\n  - `ProtectKernelDefaults=true`: Fails if any tunable differs (production safety)\n  - Default: Warns but continues (allows flexibility in test environments)\n- **Tradeoff**: Production deployments must match expectations\n\n### Resource Allocation Failures\n\n**Topology Affinity Errors**:\n- **Policy=Restricted**: Rejects pod if preferred topology unavailable\n- **Policy=BestEffort**: Accepts pod with suboptimal affinity\n- **Tradeoff**: Restricted is stricter but may reject valid workloads; BestEffort is more lenient but may cause performance degradation\n\n**CPU Static Policy Constraints**:\n- Requires nonzero CPU reservation (no shared pool exhaustion)\n- Cannot allocate fractional CPUs exclusively\n- Only supports integer CPU requests for pinning\n- **Tradeoff**: Simplicity vs. fine-grained control\n\n**Memory Static Policy Constraints**:\n- Requires reserved memory specification\n- Cannot dynamically adjust memory affinity after allocation\n- **Tradeoff**: Predictability vs. flexibility\n\n### Device Plugin Failures\n\n**Plugin Registration Timeout**:\n- Device plugins must register within startup window\n- If plugin absent: Resource unavailable to pods\n- If plugin fails: Devices become unhealthy, pods rejected\n\n**Device Allocation Failure**:\n- If plugin's Allocate() RPC fails: Container creation fails\n- Pod stays in pending state until resolved\n\n**Health Monitoring**:\n- Device manager periodically checks plugin health\n- Unhealthy plugins' resources removed from allocatable\n\n### Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) Failures\n\n**Resource Claim Allocation**:\n- DRA driver must allocate claim before pod starts\n- If allocation fails: Pod rejected at admission\n- Claim remains in allocated state for retry\n\n**Pre-allocation Timeout**:\n- PrepareDynamicResources must complete before pod moves to running\n- Long-running allocations may delay pod startup\n\n### QoS Hierarchy Edge Cases\n\n**Pod in Multiple QoS Classes**:\n- Mixed request/limit across containers determines class\n- At least one container determines pod class\n- **Tradeoff**: Simplicity; cannot mix QoS in one pod\n\n**Node Allocatable Enforcement**:\n- Pods placed under node allocatable cgroup limit\n- System services protected by separate hierarchy\n- **Concern**: If system services exceed reservation, cannot be killed\n- **Mitigation**: System reserved sizing must match actual usage\n\n### Limit Enforcement Levels\n\n**Hard Limits** (enforced immediately):\n- Memory.limit_in_bytes: OOM killer invoked if exceeded\n- cpu.cfs_quota_us: Hard CPU cap (some variance in enforcement)\n- device limits: Devices unavailable if exhausted\n\n**Soft Limits** (advisory):\n- cpu.shares: CPU weight, only enforced under contention\n- memory.soft_limit_in_bytes: Reclaimed under pressure, but memory not freed\n\n**Unrecognized Requests**:\n- Device plugins: Unknown devices silently ignored if not requested\n- Memory nodes: Requests beyond available nodes may pin to available subset\n\n### Scale Limitations\n\n**Maximum NUMA Nodes**: 8 nodes (hardcoded in topology manager, line 41 of topology_manager.go)\n- **Rationale**: Hint enumeration explodes combinatorially with NUMA nodes\n- **Impact**: Cannot enable topology manager on 16+ NUMA node systems\n\n**Container Count**:\n- Reconciliation loops iterate all active containers\n- No known hard limit, but performance degrades O(n) with containers\n\n**Device Plugin Count**:\n- Device manager maintains list of plugins\n- Each plugin connection is a goroutine\n- No hard limit, but resource usage grows with plugins\n\n## Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 1. Container Manager Policies\n\n**CPU Manager Policies** (pluggable via `--cpu-manager-policy`):\n- `none`: No management, all CPUs shared\n- `static`: Exclusive CPU pinning for integer requests\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- New policies must implement reconciliation and checkpoint logic\n- Incorrect reconciliation can cause CPU leaks or over-allocation\n- No runtime policy switching (requires restart)\n\n**Memory Manager Policies** (pluggable via `--memory-manager-policy`):\n- `none`: No management\n- `static`: NUMA node pinning\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Memory cannot be repurposed easily like CPUs\n- Failed deallocation leaves memory pinned indefinitely\n\n### 2. Topology Manager Policies\n\n**Policies** (pluggable via `--topology-manager-policy`):\n- `none`: No topology awareness\n- `best-effort`: Returns hints but doesn't reject\n- `restricted`: Rejects if preferred hint unavailable\n- `single-numa-node`: Requires single NUMA node\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Custom policies must merge hints correctly\n- Incorrect merging can allow conflicting allocations\n- Policy changes require node draining (affects all pods)\n\n### 3. Topology Manager Scopes\n\n**Scopes** (pluggable via `--topology-manager-scope`):\n- `container`: Per-container topology decisions\n- `pod`: Pod-wide topology decisions\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Scope changes affect how hints are gathered and merged\n- Changing scope requires pod restart to take effect\n\n### 4. Device Plugin Interface\n\n**Standard Plugin Registration** (Unix socket in `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/`):\n\n**Plugin Hooks**:\n- `GetDevicePluginOptions()`: Declare PreStartRequired, GetPreferredAllocationAvailable\n- `ListAndWatch()`: Stream device updates\n- `Allocate()`: Called before container starts\n- `PreStartContainer()`: Optional, called before container actually starts\n- `GetPreferredAllocation()`: Optional, called before Allocate to prefer certain devices\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Buggy plugins can hang kubelet if synchronous calls timeout\n- Plugins crashing leave processes orphaned\n- Malicious plugin could exhaust system resources\n- PreStartContainer hook runs with elevated privileges (can modify container)\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Plugin server timeout prevents indefinite hangs\n- Health checks periodically restart plugins\n- Plugin resource usage not limited (trust model)\n\n### 5. Cgroup Driver Selection\n\n**Cgroup Drivers** (pluggable via `--cgroup-driver`):\n- `cgroupfs`: Direct filesystem manipulation\n- `systemd`: Uses systemd slice/scope units\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Wrong driver selection incompatible with system\n- Mixing drivers on same node causes conflicts\n- cgroupfs has some privilege escalation vectors if misconfigured\n\n**Platform Variance**:\n- systemd driver only available on systemd systems (most modern Linux)\n- cgroupfs works on any cgroup v1 system\n- cgroup v2 unified interface works differently for both drivers\n\n### 6. QoS and Node Allocatable Customization\n\n**Node Allocatable Configuration** (via `--system-reserved`, `--kube-reserved`, `--eviction-hard`):\n- Controls how much resources reserved from pods\n- Incorrect sizing can starve system services\n- Over-reservation leaves unused capacity\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Changing reservation requires node restart\n- System services exceeding reservation cannot be evicted\n- No enforcement of actual usage vs. reservation\n\n### 7. Pod Admission Handler\n\n**PodAdmitHandler Interface** (for container manager, topology manager):\n- Called before pod enters the node\n- Can reject pod if resources unavailable\n- Runs serially for all pods being admitted\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Slow admission handlers block scheduler\n- Rejecting pods with invalid reason confuses scheduler\n- Cannot access pod's actual runtime requirements\n\n### 8. Plugin Registration Handler\n\n**PluginHandler Interface** (for device manager):\n- Called when plugin socket appears/disappears\n- Manages plugin connection lifecycle\n- Runs concurrently across plugins\n\n**Extension Risk**:\n- Plugin directory has relaxed permissions (`/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/`)\n- Malicious code can create fake plugin socket\n- Plugin can be injected at runtime (root access required, but possible)\n\n## Operational Implications\n\n### Performance Characteristics\n\n**CPU Overhead**:\n1. **Topology Manager**: Generates hints for all resources (O(number of providers \u00d7 containers))\n   - Linear in container count, exponential in NUMA nodes\n   - Evaluation happens at pod admission (synchronous, affects scheduler latency)\n\n2. **CPU Manager Reconciliation**: O(active containers) every ~5 seconds\n   - Updates only changed containers (incremental)\n   - CRI call per changed container (batching not possible)\n\n3. **Memory Manager**: Similar to CPU manager in reconciliation cost\n\n4. **QoS Update**: O(pods) to update cgroup limits\n   - Runs periodically, not per-container change\n   - Scales poorly with high pod churn\n\n**Memory Overhead**:\n- Topology manager caches hints per provider \u00d7 container (O(containers \u00d7 providers \u00d7 NUMA nodes))\n- CPU/Memory managers checkpoint to disk (small files, ~1KB per container)\n- Device manager maps all plugin devices in memory (O(devices across all plugins))\n\n### Reliability and Monitoring\n\n**Health Checks**:\n- Device manager monitors plugin health (periodic List/Watch)\n- Unhealthy plugins' resources marked unavailable\n- No automatic plugin restart (external mechanism required)\n\n**Observability**:\n- Topology manager emits `TopologyAffinityError` when pod cannot be admitted\n- Device manager logs allocation failures\n- CPU/Memory manager logs reconciliation mismatches\n- Container manager logs setup failures\n\n**Checkpointing**:\n- CPU manager checkpoints state on every Allocate/RemoveContainer\n- Memory manager checkpoints state on every Allocate/RemoveContainer\n- Checkpoint loss on kubelet restart means lost allocations (pods must be recreated)\n- Stale checkpoint can block pod from scheduling if not cleaned\n\n### Scalability Considerations\n\n**Node Density**:\n- Topology manager scales poorly beyond 100 pods with topology policies enabled\n- Hint enumeration and merging becomes bottleneck\n- Recommendation: Use `topology-manager-policy: none` for high-density nodes\n\n**Large Pod Count**:\n- QoS cgroup updates are O(pods), running periodically\n- Device allocation calls are per-pod, not batched\n- Recommendation: Monitor resource manager reconciliation latency\n\n**Device Plugins**:\n- Each plugin requires dedicated socket and connection\n- Plugins consuming large memory or CPU should be monitored separately\n- Recommend: Consolidate multiple devices into single plugin\n\n### Node Upgrades and Changes\n\n**Cgroup Version Migration** (v1 to v2):\n- Requires node drain and kubelet restart\n- Cannot change `--cgroup-driver` without drain\n- Recommendation: Migrate during maintenance window with pod eviction\n\n**Topology Manager Policy Changes**:\n- Policy changes (e.g., `none` \u2192 `restricted`) affect all pods\n- Pods with non-preferred topology may be rejected\n- Recommendation: Apply during maintenance window, monitor pod failures\n\n**Device Plugin Lifecycle**:\n- Plugins can be installed/removed without node restart\n- New plugin appears in device list after registration\n- Recommendation: Drain nodes before removing plugins\n\n**System Reserved Changes**:\n- `--system-reserved` changes require node restart\n- Over-reservation may strand resources\n- Under-reservation may crash system services\n- Recommendation: Size based on actual system usage, not estimates\n\n### Failure Recovery\n\n**Stuck Pods (Resource Allocation)**:\n- If DRA allocation fails: Pod stays pending indefinitely\n- If device unavailable: Pod stays pending\n- Recovery: Fix underlying resource issue, pod automatically retries\n\n**Cgroup Cleanup**:\n- Orphaned cgroups remain after container crash\n- Container manager handles cleanup on new pod creation\n- Manual cleanup: `cgdelete` or systemd tools\n\n**Corrupted Checkpoint**:\n- CPU/Memory manager checkpoint corruption causes allocation failures\n- Recovery: Delete checkpoint file (`cpu_manager_state`), restart kubelet\n- Risk: Newly started containers may get same CPUs (collision)\n\n### Backward Compatibility\n\n**Policy Changes**:\n- CPU policy switch (none \u2194 static) requires kubelet restart\n- Changing mid-flight could cause allocation conflicts\n- No migration path: Manual pod recreation required\n\n**Cgroup Driver Switch**:\n- Requires node drain, cgroup migration, kubelet restart\n- Existing cgroup hierarchies incompatible between drivers\n- High-risk operation\n\n**QoS Hierarchy Changes**:\n- Enabling `--cgroups-per-qos` on existing node requires pod eviction\n- No automatic migration of existing pods to QoS cgroups\n\n## Map of Important Files and Directories\n\n```\npkg/kubelet/cm/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 container_manager.go                 # Core ContainerManager interface (66-170)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 container_manager_linux.go           # Linux implementation (100-700+)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 container_manager_windows.go         # Windows implementation\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 container_manager_stub.go            # No-op implementation (for unsupported systems)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 types.go                             # CgroupManager, PodContainerManager interfaces\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 internal_container_lifecycle.go      # that:\n\n1. **Layers abstractions** from system cgroups up to Kubernetes QoS classes\n2. **Coordinates multiple managers** (CPU, Memory, Device, Topology) via hint-based negotiation\n3. **Maintains checkpoints** to survive kubelet restarts without losing allocations\n4. **Provides extension points** (policies, plugins, drivers) with clear security boundaries\n5. **Balances flexibility with predictability** through policy selection at node configuration time\n\nSuccess depends on correct sizing of system reserved resources, appropriate policy selection for workload characteristics, and understanding the tradeoffs between strict affinity requirements vs. flexible resource allocation.\n\n",

# Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide

## Overview

The kubelet container manager subsystem is responsible for managing container resources, enforcing Quality of Service (QoS) classes, and coordinating resource allocation across CPU, memory, and device plugins. It sits at the intersection of pod scheduling, container runtime execution, and system resource enforcement on the node.

The container manager operates at several levels:
- **System level**: Managing system containers and daemon processes
- **Node level**: Enforcing node allocatable reservations and capacity limits
- **Pod level**: Creating pod cgroups and managing QoS hierarchies
- **Container level**: Allocating exclusive resources and updating runtime constraints

## Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

### Purpose
The container manager ensures that:
1. Container resource requests and limits are enforced through cgroup mechanisms
2. Resources are allocated according to pod QoS classes (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort)
3. Topology-aware resource allocation is coordinated across multiple resource managers
4. Device plugins can register and provide custom resources
5. Dynamic resource allocation can be managed through DRA framework
6. System services and kubelet process have protected resource reservations

### Boundaries

**Upstream Dependencies:**
- **Kubelet Core** (`pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go`): Initializes the container manager during startup and calls it for pod admission and container lifecycle hooks
- **Pod Workers** (`pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`): Request container lifecycle operations through the manager
- **Runtime Service** (CRI): Container manager updates container resources through CRI calls to adjust CPU/memory constraints
- **cAdvisor** (`pkg/kubelet/cadvisor/`): Provides machi
... (truncated)
